		<h1 class="entry-title"><a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2020/06/whole-lemon-meringue-pie-bars/" rel="bookmark">whole lemon meringue pie&nbsp;bars</a></h1>
		<div class="entry-meta">
			<span class="posted-on"><time class="entry-date published" datetime="2020-06-23T14:40:43-05:00">June 23, 2020</time><time class="updated" datetime="2020-07-15T12:44:41-05:00">July 15, 2020</time></span><span class="byline"> by <span class="author vcard"><a class="url fn n" href="https://smittenkitchen.com/author/debsk/">deb</a></span></span>
			<span id="smittenkitchen-jump-links" class="jump-links">
				Jump to 				<a class="recipe-jump-link" href="recipe">recipe, </a>
				<a href="#comments">comments</a>
			</span>
		</div><!-- .entry-meta -->

	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		
	<div class="smittenkitchen-print-hide">
		<p>I&#8217;ve apparently been wanting to make lemon meringue pie bars for at least eight years, as per my decade-plus log of everything I want to cook. Three different times I&#8217;ve tried to draft a recipe but I always got stuck on how much was involved, both in three separate cooking processes and eggs, just so many eggs. Whole eggs in the lemon portion, egg whites for the topping&#8230; it just felt like a lot, if not a dealbreaker, enough reason for me to pause on the idea until I had a more efficient way to approach it. </p>
<p><span id="more-45308"></span><br />
<a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026303461/in/photostream" title="grahams or digestives, sugar, salt, butter"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i1.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026303461_e98f2e6cde_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="grahams or digestives, sugar, salt, butter" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026302841/in/photostream" title="cold butter crumb crust"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i1.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026302841_18bd12fe9e_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="cold butter crumb crust" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026563397/in/photostream" title="press-in crust"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i0.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026563397_e6301c91b9_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="press-in crust" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026303301/in/photostream" title="ready to par-bake"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i2.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026303301_16fbc90aab_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="ready to par-bake" data-recalc-dims="1"></a></p>
<p>I found it in Susan Spungen&#8217;s (who you might remember from this <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2019/11/perfect-apple-tarte-tatin/">Perfect Tarte Tatin</a>) latest cookbook, <a href="https://amzn.to/37Qje3y">Open Kitchen</a>, which focuses on cooking for casual entertaining, a distant memory these days but I do love the breezy-feeling recipes here. Spungen is a recipe developer and food stylist and I know that the latter connotes images of a person moving parsley around with tweezers or using dental grip to keep a cookie in place on set, in reality, most food stylists I know arrive at work and are handed a stack of recipes that may or may not even work, which they have to cook and plate them in a very short window of time. The food stylists I know are very good cooks, skilled at cutting to the chase of a recipe. Spungen&#8217;s book benefits from this. </p>
<p><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50025760158/in/photostream" title="eggs, butter, lemon"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i1.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50025760158_bdbd883e5f_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="eggs, butter, lemon" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026563767/in/photostream" title="lemon, butter, yolks, sugar"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i0.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026563767_9ffbf1cc1e_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="lemon, butter, yolks, sugar" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50025760793/in/photostream" title="blend until very smooth"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i1.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50025760793_806a9a744f_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="blend until very smooth" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50025759303/in/photostream" title="pour onto crust and bake"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i0.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50025759303_4f642601e3_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="pour onto crust and bake" data-recalc-dims="1"></a></p>
<p>Spungen uses one of my favorite ways to make lemon bars (see: <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2009/02/whole-lemon-tart/">Whole Lemon Tart</a> in the archives or Whole Lemon Bars in The Smitten Kitchen Cookbook) &#8212; with one whole lemon, rather than the fresh-squeezed juice of half a dozen &#8212; to make a complexly flavored lemon bar. Only yolks go into the lemon portion, and only whites in the meringue in an efficiency of ingredients and processes I found deeply soothing. The resulting bars are wildly delicious &#8212; the sweet meringue, toasted like a marshmallow, is the perfect balance for the intense lemon bar. There are still three things to prep, but I add a few shortcuts &#8212; I make my crumb crust and whole lemon curd with cold butter, and I fast-cool things in the freezer &#8212; that make it more efficient. The bars you&#8217;ll get to eat when you&#8217;re done are fully worth it. </p>
<p><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026322851/in/photostream" title="beat the egg whites and sugar"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i1.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026322851_fa647f7cde_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="beat the egg whites and sugar" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50025780518/in/photostream" title="whipped meringue"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i2.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50025780518_2f7316115f_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="whipped meringue" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50025780608/in/photostream" title="swirl the meringue, then toast"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i2.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50025780608_12ce78d470_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="swirl the meringue, then toast" data-recalc-dims="1"></a><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026302256/in/photostream" title="whole lemon meringue pie bars"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i1.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026302256_1f90a1edf0_n.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#038;ssl=1" width="320" height="213" alt="whole lemon meringue pie bars" data-recalc-dims="1"></a></p>
<p><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/smitten/50026301941/in/photostream" title="whole lemon meringue pie bars"><img loading="lazy" src="https://i0.wp.com/live.staticflickr.com/65535/50026301941_64d1d343e8_z.jpg?resize=640%2C427&#038;ssl=1" width="640" height="427" alt="whole lemon meringue pie bars" data-recalc-dims="1"></a></p>
<p><font size="3"></p>

<div class="hrecipe h-recipe jetpack-recipe" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/Recipe"><h3 class="p-name jetpack-recipe-title fn" itemprop="name">Whole Lemon Meringue Pie Bars</h3><ul class="jetpack-recipe-meta"><li class="jetpack-recipe-servings p-yield yield" itemprop="recipeYield"><strong>Servings: </strong>12 to 16</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-time">
				<time itemprop="totalTime" datetime="1 hour, plus cooling times"><strong>Time:</strong> <span class="time">1 hour, plus cooling times</span></time>
			</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-source"><strong>Source: </strong><a href="https://amzn.to/37Qje3y">Open Kitchen, by Susan Spungen</a></li><li class="jetpack-recipe-print"><a href="#">Print</a></li></ul><div class="jetpack-recipe-content"> </p>
<p><div class="jetpack-recipe-notes">Let&#8217;s talk about lemons: Spungen recommends a Meyer lemon for the whole lemon but I found in working on my own whole lemon bars that regular (Eureka) lemons were just fine so long as they&#8217;re not too large (4 to 4.5 ounces is ideal) and the skin isn&#8217;t too thick. Cut the lemon in half and take a look at the thickness of the pith (white layer) of the skin. Does it look thick to you, perhaps even 1/4-inch thick or larger? If so, go ahead and remove the skin only from one half of the lemon before proceeding. If it looks normal or not especially thick, you’ll be just fine.</div> </p>
<p><div class="jetpack-recipe-ingredients"><ul>
<h5>Crust</h5><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">9 whole graham cracker sheets (1 sleeve), broken into pieces or 1 1/2 cups (150 grams) crumbs</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">1/4 cup (50 grams) granulated sugar</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">Large pinch of salt</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">5 tablespoons unsalted butter, cut into cubes</li>
<h5>Filling</h5><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">1 whole (preferably organic) lemon, any variety (see Note), scrubbed</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">Juice of 1/2 lemon</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">4 large egg yolks</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">8 tablespoons (4 ounces or 115 grams) unsalted butter, cut into cubes</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">1 cup (200 grams) granulated sugar</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">1 teaspoon pure vanilla extract (optional; I skip it)</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">Pinch of salt</li>
<h5>Meringue</h5><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">4 large egg whites</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">1 cup (200 grams) granulated sugar</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">1/2 teaspoon pure vanilla extract</li><li class="jetpack-recipe-ingredient p-ingredient ingredient" itemprop="recipeIngredient">Pinch of salt</li></ul></div> </p>
<p><div class="jetpack-recipe-directions e-instructions"><b>Make the crust:</b> Heat your oven to 350F [180C]. Line an 8-by-8-inch [20-by-20-cm] baking pan with two pieces of parchment trimmed to fit, going in both directions, with some extra hanging over for easy removal of the bars later. </p>
<p>Place the graham crackers, sugar, and salt in the bowl of a food processor and process until the fine crumbs form. Add the cold butter and pulse until the cold butter blends into the crumbs. It should look and feel like wet sand. Transfer to the prepared pan and mix it up with your hands  to make sure the butter is well distributed. Press into the pan, going up the sides a bit, and bake for 10 minutes, or until just golden. Let cool while you make the filling.</p>
<p><b>Make the filling:</b> [See Note up top for using different lemons.] Trim the stem end of the whole lemon and cut it into thin slices. Remove any seeds. Add to a food processor or blender jar (preferably a high speed blender) along with the lemon juice, egg yolks, butter, sugar, vanilla (if using), and salt and blend until very smooth, scraping down the sides as needed. Pour over the crust (it’s ok if it’s still warm) and bake for 30 minutes, or until it is bubbling and browning around the edges. It won’t look at all set, and might even look like a total mess (unevenly browned or bubbly), but it will set up as it cools. Place on a cooling rack. After about 10 minutes, run a small, sharp knife around the edges. Cool completely, then chill until coldm (I sped this up in the freezer). When completely chilled, carefully remove the parchment and, using a spatula, transfer to a small baking sheet (you can do this just before adding the topping &#8212; I missed this step and regretted it because you want the paper off before you try to toast the top or it will &#8212; whoops &#8212; burn). </p>
<p><b>Make the meringue:</b> An hour or so before serving, make the topping. Combine the egg whites, sugar, vanilla, and salt in the metal bowl of a stand mixer and set over a pan of simmering water. Keep the mixture moving, using a whisk or the whisk attachment, until the sugar is completely melted and it’s hot to the touch (or 160F). Transfer to a stand mixer and beat on high speed until glossy and very stiff, 2 to 3 minutes. Transfer to the top of the lemon bars, smooth out, and use a large serving fork to create a pattern in the meringue, or the back of a spoon or offset spatula to make swirls like you see here. </p>
<p><b>Finish the bars:</b> When you’re ready to finish, use a kitchen torch or your oven&#8217;s broiler to brown the meringue. Refrigerate until ready to serve. Use a knife dipped into hot water to cut bars into 12 to 16 squares, depending on how large you want them.</div> </p>
<p></div></div>

	<li class="comment even depth-2" id="comment-1586476">
		<article id="div-comment-1586476" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Chelsea									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>(1) For the crust, you can put the crackers in a ziplock/plastic bag and crush well before combining with the other ingredients. (Or any way of crushing cookies well and uniformly would work, I suppose). (2) For the filling, I think you either (a) want to find a lemon filling recipe that doesn&#8217;t use the lemon rinds and substitute that or (b) if you have a blender, you might be able to get away with that. (3) For the meringue, I&#8217;m pretty sure you can just use a whisk and whisk and whisk until it forms stiff peaks.</p>
			</div>

				<b class="fn author-name">
											Mimi									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I think the filling level is pretty proportionate but I think you’d still get a pretty nice effect with just half the meringue. </p>
<p>My suggestion, however, would be to make more crust and go higher up on the sides with it so it’s more pie-like. That way the majority of the pieces will have extra crust (like 75% if cut into 16 pieces) and their will be a few “normal” middle pieces. </p>
<p>Either method would retain the integrity of the bars.</p>
			</div>

			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Angela Murray									</b>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>To determine how much to increase the original recipe to use a larger pan, use this equation<br />
(13 × 9)÷(8×8)=(117)÷(64)=1.8 So increase the recipe by 1.8 times. Easiest if you use grams. So if you double it, it will just be a thicker batch.</p>
			</div>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Two questions: </p>
<p>1. Could you share more photos/descriptive logistics as to how to handle the bowl, pan of water, and stand mixer when making the meringue? Do you use a bowl that&#8217;s shorter than the stand mixer bowl, move the stand mixer over to the stove and hold everything in place while mixing over the simmering water? And then transfer to the stand mixer bowl for the whisking/whipping stage? Or is this all easier with a hand mixer? (Sorry, that was a lot of questions in one) </p>
<p>2. It would be a totally different bar, but I&#8217;m dreaming of this with a chocolate filling instead of lemon, so it&#8217;s like a s&#8217;mores bar. Would the filling from your chocolate tart recipe work? </p>
<p>Thank you as always for beautiful and delicious recipes!</p>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Hi Fran, For 1., you&#8217;d place the stand mixer&#8217;s bowl over the pot of simmering water and whisk by hand until it&#8217;s about 160 degrees, then place that bowl back into the stand mixer for the next part. I just checked, and the first few Google Images for &#8216;stand mixer bowl double boiler&#8217; show the right idea. Hope that&#8217;s helpful!</p>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Hi Fran &#8212; In a bit, I&#8217;ll share an Instagram Story demo which I can link to here and you can see how I did it. Also, I realize I didn&#8217;t add my notes in that part. I just use a handmixer. So, I beat it for a few minutes over the water, transfer the bowl to a towel, and continue beating it until it&#8217;s thick. It&#8217;s a bit more straightforward.</p>
<p>I love the s&#8217;mores idea. The chocolate tart would work but I am tempted to point you to one way way way back in the archives, <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2006/12/chocolate-concise/">in this post</a>. The filling was so rich and more ganache-ish, which feels closer to a s&#8217;more texture. Let me know if you try it. Also, btw! There&#8217;s a <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2008/06/smore-pie/">s&#8217;more pie</a> in the archives too, but I think it needs some streamlining.</p>

			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											JP									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>The problem with Meyer lemons is that they are not tart enough for a dessert like this.  After all, they are a cross between the Eureka lemon and the mandarin orange.  I have made lemon desserts with them and been disappointed.  Add on a very sweet meringue and, at least in my opinion, there is not enough contrast.  Meyer lemons are really popular right now, and here in CA they are very easy to find, but if you really want to taste lemon, stick with Eureka, that plain old grocery store lemon and go with Deb&#8217;s instructions about the rind, which can be much thicker than a Meyer.</p>
			</div>

				<p>This may be the first thing I make when I have an oven again (oven died in January, kitchen reno happening as I type . . .). I often use italian meringue for anything that won&#8217;t be completely consumed in a day&#8211;another alternative, if you need to make it ahead of time, is to make italian meringue &#8220;drops&#8221; and bake them for awhile in a very very low oven, then place on top when you want to serve and torch them then.</p>

				<p>I want to love this recipe for sooo many reasons, but the bottom crust and filling was cloying and gooey in a greasy way. Maybe I did something wrong??  If not, next time less butter in the crust, less butter in the filling unless I add more ingredients. In comparing this to your whole lemon bars (which are my favorites), I want to try whole eggs and maybe the cornstarch. What I loved about this recipe: the meringue was sensational and any chance to use my blowtorch is a win! The bars were beautiful &amp; the taste was super lemony.</p>

	<li class="comment odd alt depth-2" id="comment-1594963">
		<article id="div-comment-1594963" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Beth S									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Made them again a few days later, using Deb&#8217;s original whole lemon bar recipe and was far happier. I doubled the recipe and put them in an 9&#215;13 glass pan without parchment. After cooling the base and filling, I ran a sharp knife around the pan and then made the meringue. The bars were 100% better and the meringue on top was more proportional to the distinct layers on the bottom-no mushy, sticky combined crust and lemon layer!  PS Cutting and removal was a breeze.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1588147">
		<article id="div-comment-1588147" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Ree									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Oh man! Seeing this recipe on here this morning was a dream come true of mine. Also the first time I&#8217;ve made this kind of meringue myself before! (Is it Swiss? Italian? I can never tell the difference). </p>
<p>Anyway, a few notes: This was WAY sweeter than I expected, mostly because I expect recipes coming from Smitten to be dialed back on the sweetness, for the most part! I had an instinct to reduce the sugar in the crust or the filling but went against it, which I feel was a mistake. The final result is of course delicious, but tooth-achingly sweet with not as much contrast between the literal heaps of meringue and the much thinner lemon filling. This also may have been because I made the recipe as written, with graham crackers and with the vanilla, as opposed to how Deb made them. </p>
<p>Second, I also found the instructions on making the meringue a little confusing at first. I basically put my stand mixer bowl on top of a pot filled almost halfway with water, and vigorously whisked with a long balloon whisk. A hand mixer would be great, but I don&#8217;t have one! I then moved to my stand mixer, as stated. Ended up working great! </p>
<p>Thanks for the recipe, and can&#8217;t wait to make again when I can pawn some of the sweetness off on friends :)</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1588618">
		<article id="div-comment-1588618" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											emily									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made these yesterday with no modifications to the recipe. However, I only have a ceramic baking pan, and it is thicker than a regular metal baking pan. </p>
<p>Like other commenters, I was surprised by how sweet these bars are. If I were to make them again I think I&#8217;d take the sugar out of the crust and try to halve the sugar in the filling. My crust also became gloopy and gummy &#8211; you can scoop it out of the dish with a spoon but definitely no hope of cutting it into bars. I think my thicker pan may have contributed to the lack of &#8220;crustiness&#8221; in the crust. My meringue also never got stiff even after nearly ten minutes of beating, but it was getting thicker so I just spread it once it was thick enough to hold a texture. I made a linear pattern with a fork that came out quite pretty after a quick broil! </p>
<p>I will say that I&#8217;m operating in a rental kitchen, so not the best equipment, and it was pretty warm in here without AC so perhaps that&#8217;s why my meringue had issues. I love the &#8220;whole lemon&#8221; idea, as the flavor was more complex with that element of bitterness. I also appreciated how efficient the recipe is &#8211; no wasted egg yolks or whites! I think I may try making this filling and swirling it into a cheesecake. </p>
<p>Overall the result wasn&#8217;t 100% what I&#8217;d hoped but certainly has elements I would use again. Interesting recipe, thanks Deb!</p>
			</div>

				<p>I’ve made an Arizona Sunshine Lemon Pie (I live in the Phoenix area).  It uses a lwhole, seeded lemon, is made in the blender, poured into a pie crust and baked. Very easy and really delicious.  We prefer it to any lemon meringue pie we’ve ever tried.  It just uses a large lemon, 4 eggs, 1/2 cup melted butter, 1 tsp vanilla and 1 1/2 cups of sugar (and, of course, a pie crust!).</p>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I’m going to be honest I stan 99% of SK recipes but this one did not work for me at all. My crust got burned, the filling was inedibly bitter, and the meringue wound up salty (this one is my fault, because I should have known better than to use a full pinch of Morton). I wound up feeling like I should have not bothered parbaking the crust and should have just used a combination of zest and juice rather than trying to put the whole lemon in there. It’s weird because each element was very tasty before getting baked. But despite 2 1/4 cups of sugar the whole thing was so bitter sour and salty that I had to throw it away. Clearly I missed something here because I see a lot of comments saying it was very sweet. Pretty disappointed so many ingredients went to waste</p>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1589479">
		<article id="div-comment-1589479" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Rebecca									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made this and the whole family agreed it was delicious. Worth the steps. Some of us have celiac disease so I used Pamela&#8217;s honey graham GF crackers and the crust was delicious. I was short on time so I had to put the bars in the freezer (pre-meringue) before they were fully cooled, and it seemed to be okay. No parchment paper so I did the meringue in the original 8 by 8 dish (which I had greased really well with butter before baking the crust) and that worked fine. I had been confused about whether there needed to be a lapse in time between making the meringue and broiling the top &#8212; I did not wait, and that was also fine. Definitely watch it closely &#8212; I should have pulled it out from under the broiler about 45 seconds earlier. Thank you! The whole lemon trick is very cool.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1590388">
		<article id="div-comment-1590388" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											DV									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>These bars were delicious, just a bit confusing to make for me. I used Annie’s bunny honey graham’s for the crust; they are very sweet so I didn’t add sugar &#8211; worked fine. The lemon layer was delicious; I mixed everything in a food processor (took a while for the filling to get creamy, but it did). I used an average sized lemon with 3/4 cup sugar (instead of 1 cup); it was the perfect balance between sweet/tart. The meringue was simple to make; took a bit longer for mine to form stiff peaks but otherwise was an easier task than I feared. It makes a lot but it was fun to pile it all on top of the lemon filling and is so marshmallow-y delicious. I liked the ratios of the layers. I don’t have a torch so I browned the meringue for about 1 minute under the broiler; worked fine, just not quite as pretty as a torch.<br />
So for those who thought the recipe was too sweet:<br />
Taste the graham crackers or cookies you’re using for the crust; if they’re super sweet (which most of them are), adjust or eliminate the sugar.<br />
The lemon layer worked fine with 3/4 cup of sugar instead of 1 full cup (but that will depend on the size/bitterness of your lemon).<br />
I used all the sugar called for in the meringue; we thought it was just right.<br />
The bars have kept very well in the fridge for 3 days.</p>
			</div>

			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Patty									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made these on Saturday and I’m not sure they’re worth the work. Despite using a thin skinned lemon and a high speed blender, I had to strain bits of rind out of the filling to get it smooth. Some of the crust ended up in the filling, which I think may have been because it was too warm when I filled it.  Filling ran under the parchment and the bars were hard to separate form the paper.<br />
When I finally finished, they were ok enough for me to try again at some point (with less sugar) but overall I was disappointed with the outcome vs the work  (and surprised because I’ve never had a less than fabulous outcome from this site!)</p>
			</div>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Theoretically, but with a couple caveats. One, I don&#8217;t find whole-lime desserts as enjoyable as whole-lemon, but that just might be my personal tastes. Two, the taste of key lime is from the combination of lime juice + sweetened condensed milk, see this <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2015/01/key-lime-pie/">Key Lime Pie</a> and/or <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2008/01/key-lime-cheesecake/">Key Lime Cheesecake</a>. Three, you might instead use <a href="https://smittenkitchen.com/2006/09/in-praise-of-the-pocket-sized/">this lime curd</a> for the lemon part, which is a little closer to the lemon here but without the whole rind.</p>
			</div>

											David									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>LOVED these. And I also learned what &#8220;pith&#8221; is! </p>
<p>I did cut back the sugar on the crust by half and saw no problem, cut the filling sugar back a little bit as well. I agree this is pretty sweet even with this, but meringue you can&#8217;t mess with. Will be trying a chocolate version to make this a full on smore experiment.</p>
<p>One thing I didn&#8217;t get is the parchment removal, or the need for it in the first place (is this Deb&#8217;s OCD on clean up haha). Why not just grease the pan? You eliminate the dangerous possibility of destroying the entire thing by taking it out and putting it back in. What I ended up doing by accident was cutting around the edge which cut thru the parchment on the side and I just pulled the sides out. But it did mess up the edges, so next time I&#8217;m going with buttering the pan and simplifying it altogether.</p>
			</div>

											<a href="http://smittenkitchen.com">deb</a>

			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>For two reasons, you want to remove the parchment. One, it really, really sticks to the meringue as it sets so it&#8217;s best to separate it sooner. And two, it will burn (like, with tiny flames) when you torch or broil the top. Glad you enjoyed the bars!</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1592739">
		<article id="div-comment-1592739" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Erica									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>These lemon meringue pie bars are delicious! Based on comments about them being overly sweet, I halved the sugar in the crust and used 3/4 c. sugar in the filling. It was great, but next time I will probably leave out the sugar in the crust, and reduce the sugar in the filling to 2/3 c.<br />
I don&#8217;t have a food processor, but do have a Vitamix blender, so I made the crust using the dry container, and made the filling using the regular Vitamix container. Worked perfectly!</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1592913">
		<article id="div-comment-1592913" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Femke									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>The key lime pie being one of my favourites on the site, I had to try this recipe. I halved it and had to substitute the graham crackers for digestive biscuits, since we don&#8217;t have graham crackers here. Reading the comments, I reduced the sugar in the lemon filling by an extra 50%, used a whole small organic lemon plus juice of half a lime (what I had lying around), and this worked out perfectly. Making the Swiss meringue was my first time but was easy, and it appears to keeping well in the fridge (day three now). My base was the right texture and did not mix with the lemon layer, as some others experienced.</p>
<p>All in all, relatively easy, good-looking and very tasty recipe, but the sugar in the lemon filling should be reduced by half (and maybe leave it out of the base).</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1593120">
		<article id="div-comment-1593120" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Virginia									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>A word of advice &#8211; allow yourself plenty of time for these to chill before removing parchment!  Mine seemed reasonably set when I took them out of the oven &#8211; a little loose in the middle but per the recipe sounded like they would set up.  I rushed the cooling process in the freezer but definitely not for long enough &#8211; when I attempted to remove the parchment, it was partly stuck to the crust due to some of the filling running under the crust.  Disaster &#8211; the filling was almost liquid in the middle and it went everywhere! I patched it together, added the meringue, toasted it under the broiler, and it pretty much had to be eaten with a spoon.  The crust and meringue were delicious, but the filling was waaaayyyy too bitter for my lemon-loving family. I used an average grocery store lemon with pretty thin rind, but I guess next time I&#8217;ll find a Eureka if possible.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1594203">
		<article id="div-comment-1594203" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Michellers									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made this with mixed results. Didn&#8217;t feel like washing my food processor so bashed the graham crackers in a baggie, added sugar, salt, and cubes of butter and bashed it some more until it was the right texture. Lemons were small so used 1-1/2 and I whirled the lemon mixture on high in my blender, very satisfying. Didn&#8217;t want to wash my stand mixer either so used a hand mixer on high for the meringue and it worked fine.</p>
<p>I had issues with my overhanging parchment flopping down onto the lemon layer in the oven&#8211;super annoying, would use foil next time.</p>
<p>Graham cracker a little too cooked after 10 minutes alone and then 30 with filling, so next time would cook it a little less in both steps.</p>
<p>Thought making the meringue was fun but taste-wise it was too much and too sweet&#8211;just my personal preference, so I would half the topping recipe. Which would ruin the symmetry of 4 yolks and 4 whites :-)</p>
<p>Overall, it is tasty but the whole not quite as good as its parts.</p>
			</div>

			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Leslie									</b>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Made these for family of pie lovers and they were a fantastic hit. Based on others&#8217; comments I didn&#8217;t add any sugar to the Graham cracker mix in crust, and cut back to 1/2 cup in the filling, and it was just perfect. Still plenty sweet. Used regular eureka lemons. Also baked on regular aluminum foil (not non-stick) and just trimmed off the excess on the sides (we didn&#8217;t need a fancy presentation). 10/10 would make again, the lemon flavor really is deeper and more complex than any other I&#8217;ve tried. Perfect proportions in an 8&#215;8.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-1594867">

			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											SC									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Deb, this is the first time I’ve commented on your blog but your site has been my go-to for all recipes (especially desserts) since covid has forced me to wfh. Looking through the site for ideas on what to make next has been a fun distraction from the wfh life with two toddlers and a (also forced to wfh) spouse. </p>
<p>I’ve never wanted to comment on your blog until I read your article in the NYT today about choosing either a child or a job, because you can’t have both during covid. I cannot agree more with you! I am also coming from a place of privilege, as I’ve been able to hire a nanny to take care of my children most of the week while my husband and I work from home offices (which were once bedrooms). I can’t imagine what it would be like if we couldn’t afford help AND we had to go into work &#8211; a situation that too many essential workers find themselves in. I completely agree with you that we need a solution in the fall that works for two-income households (and single working parents). </p>
<p>I know you know you’re not alone in your struggle to balance family and career in the covid world, but I wanted to chime in and say that I also stand with you. I had no idea that you were also struggling as a published writer and successful blogger &#8211; and knowing that you are has also made me empathize with you even more. Your work has been one of the few bright spots in my lockdown life, and I really hope that you don’t need to choose between your family and your children.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1595196">
		<article id="div-comment-1595196" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Nikki									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made this for my Mom who is very picky about lemon sweets, her favorite pie is lemon meringue and favorite sweet lemon bars but they have to be just so. These were perfect and believe me, she would tell me to my face if they weren&#8217;t! </p>
<p>They combine lemon meringue pie and lemon bars well, although neither of those have a graham cracker crust I think the crust is really good and helps add a different dimension to the recipe. </p>
<p>Thanks for the tip on cutting some of the skin off if it&#8217;s too thick. I think I ended up adding some of it back in and added more lemon juice than it called for but I just kept tasting for the best balance of tartness. </p>
<p>The meringue on top even convinced some non-lemon lovers to try this out and they loved the marshmallowey topping.</p>
<p>I will definitely be making these again, it was definitely easier than lemon meringue pie and more flavorful than lemon bars.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1598765">
		<article id="div-comment-1598765" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Marnie									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Adding to the chorus of thank-yous for the NYT piece. And most especially THANK YOU for calling out how the whole debate treats teachers as even more expendable than working parents. So few of these articles recognize the absurd risk to which teachers will be subjected if schools reopen without something approaching hospital-level protection. I recognize that as of now, it seems that children are not the “silent super-spreaders” everyone thought they’d be, but they can still spread un-super-ly. And there are teachers who are high risk, or who have high-risk people in their bubble. I’m as desperate to see my kiddos as anyone &#8211; first thing I learned in my teaching program was, you have to reach a child before you can teach that child &#8211; but not at the expense of my own health (hi, auto-immune disease!). And I have two kids of my own &#8211; kinder and pre-K &#8211; and I desperately want them to forge relationships with their own teachers before we inevitably return to distance learning. But again, not at the expense of their &#8211; or my, or my husband’s &#8211; health. Or, God forbid, at the expense of any of our lives.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1599695">
		<article id="div-comment-1599695" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Maria									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made these today and they were lovely, but I have maybe underprocessed the lemon filling (did it in the food processor, my blender is not that great) and they were a bit bitter. I also followed the advice of some of the commenters here and removed about 50g of sugar from the filling &#8211; it was not the best idea in combination with my slightly too bitter lemon zest. I skipped the sugar in the crust and used whole wheat digestives &#8211; did not miss it there.<br />
Oh well I&#8217;ll know next time and use the blender. :) They were a big hit.<br />
I didn&#8217;t use parchment paper because I had to take them to a family gathering and couldn&#8217;t figure out how to get them back into the pan, not burn the paper, and use the meringue torch before going on the bus with them.<br />
Even without the parchment they cut like a dream using a knife dipped in warm water.<br />
But lesson learned &#8211; will not reduce the sugar next time.</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-1599988">
		<article id="div-comment-1599988" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Jennifer									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Deb, I LOVED the NYT essay &#8212; thank you for so coherently saying what should be obvious &#8212; but is hard to communicate clearly when we&#8217;re all stressed and sleep-deprived.</p>
<p>These bars &#8230; I understand what happened (and it&#8217;s obvious from the photos) but 4 egg whites make a LOT of meringue.  Also, the bars need to be fully chilled (not just cooled on the counter) to actually set. We had them cooled (but not cold) and they were a mess. The next morning, one could actually imagine them as bars, but they still had an insane meringue layer: if I do them again, I may hold back an egg white for a more balanced set of layers.</p>
			</div>

				<p>It might have needed longer. I know that egg whites can get overbeaten, but I find it less likely to happen with a cooked meringue like this. Mine hit stiff/firm and then stay there. 											Jen									</b>

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Hi Deb! I&#8217;ve been making your recipes for the past thirteen years, and sadly, this one was a huge fail. You are my go-to source for my recipes, from birthday cake extravaganzas to weeknight dinners. Everything looked and smelled delicious, and the graham cracker crust and meringue were perfect. The curd set up well, but it was inedible! I tested out my lemon before I processed it, and the lemon pith wasn&#8217;t very thick nor did it taste excessively bitter. Because of the bitterness in the curd, even with the delicious meringue and graham cracker crust, we had to throw out the entire dessert. I was so disappointed.</p>

			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I just made these tonight- super easy. I did it mostly while on the phone! You&#8217;re not kidding when you say that the lemon filling bakes up ugly. I thought for sure I goofed somewhere, but I pressed on anyway, and what do you know? It set up perfectly. </p>
<p>For anyone else in Florida or a similar climate, I would add that meringue just doesn&#8217;t want to whip up in heat or humidity. You&#8217;re not doing anything wrong if your meringue refuses to fully form stiff peaks, it&#8217;s just mother nature. It still comes out just as lovely, if a little softer.</p>
<p>I also made this in a similar-volume ceramic baking dish (don&#8217;t have an appropriately sized metal baking pan) and it was fine. I didn&#8217;t even take the bars out, I just left them in there for serving and all. The first piece is a messy cut, but the rest pop out as you cut them just fine.</p>
			</div>

			<footer class="comment-footer comment-metadata">
				<time 2020-07-26T22:40:36-05:00 class="comment-time">

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I made these today because I needed a project, and my were they a project!!  Two things: I have burned graham cracker crusts in the past, so I’m cautious, but I think I pulled this one out too early (8 min), as it seems to not be integrous at all.  Second, I really wish you had been a little more explicit about how quickly it would go when you suggested sticking it under the broiler. I popped them in, washed a few dishes, opened the door, and the entire thing was in flames!  I pulled it out with fire literally leaping into the air!  Once the fire went out, I was able to carefully remove the blackened top layer of the meringue, but they look like crap now :). They taste like lemon graham mush, pretty disappointing for a whole afternoon!</p>

									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>Curdled appearance is fine. Soft might have needed more baking time to firm up &#8212; there&#8217;s so much variation between the crumbs of different graham brands that it can take a little adjusting. How were they from the fridge?</p>
			</div>

	<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 i-made-this" id="comment-2015085">
		<article id="div-comment-2015085" class="comment-body">
			<div class="comment-author vcard">
				<b class="fn author-name">
											Rebecca Richardson									</b>
			</div><!-- .vcard -->

			<div class="comment-content">
				<p>I had similar problems to others &#8212; a soggy crust (maybe a result of the crust not going high enough, so the curd gets &#8220;behind&#8221; it and starts to mix in?), then a too-bitter curd, then a long time getting the meringue mixture up to 160! Even using a thin-skinned Meyer lemon proved too bitter a note. I think next time I&#8217;d just use some zest and stick to the lemon juice as the main lemony note. Sad to have to throw out the time/ingredients, but afraid it was a bust for me!</p>
			</div>

			<footer class="comment-footer comment-metadata">
				<time 2021-04-09T00:48:23-05:00 class="comment-time">
